<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Kate Winslet</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint nomobile"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><img class="flaggedrevs-icon" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/doc-magnify.png" alt="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page." title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page." /><img id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" class="fr-toggle-arrow" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/arrow-down.png" style="display:none;" alt="show/hide details" /></div>
<div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails-wrapper" style="position:relative;"><div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails" class="flaggedrevs_short_details" style="display:none">This is the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pending_changes" title="Wikipedia:Pending changes">latest accepted revision</a>, <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Log&amp;type=review&amp;page=Kate_Winslet">reviewed</a> on <i>28 September 2018</i>.</div>

3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Awards</th><td>
<a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Kate_Winslet" title="List of awards and nominations received by Kate Winslet">Full list</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Kate Elizabeth Winslet</b>, <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:100%;"><a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></span> (born 5 October 1975) is an English actress. She is particularly known for her work in period dramas and tragedies, and is often drawn to portraying troubled women. Winslet is the recipient of <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Kate_Winslet" title="List of awards and nominations received by Kate Winslet">several accolades</a>, including three <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">British Academy Film Awards</a>, and is among the few performers to have won <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_won_Academy,_Emmy,_Grammy,_and_Tony_Awards#Three_competitive_awards" title="List of people who have won Academy, Emmy, Grammy, and Tony Awards">Academy, Emmy, and Grammy Awards</a>.
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading, Berkshire</a>, Winslet studied drama at the <a href="/wiki/Redroofs_Theatre_School" title="Redroofs Theatre School">Redroofs Theatre School</a>. Her first screen appearance, at the age of 15, was in the British television series <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Season" title="Dark Season">Dark Season</a></i> (1991). She made her film debut playing a teenage murderess in <i><a href="/wiki/Heavenly_Creatures" title="Heavenly Creatures">Heavenly Creatures</a></i> (1994), and received her first <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">BAFTA Award</a> for playing <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Dashwood" title="Marianne Dashwood">Marianne Dashwood</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Sense_and_Sensibility_(film)" title="Sense and Sensibility (film)">Sense and Sensibility</a></i> (1995). Global stardom followed soon after with her leading role in the epic romance <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (1997). It was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">highest-grossing film</a> of all time to that point, after which she eschewed parts in blockbusters in favour of critically acclaimed but little-seen period pieces, including <i><a href="/wiki/Quills" title="Quills">Quills</a></i> (2000) and <i><a href="/wiki/Iris_(2001_film)" title="Iris (2001 film)">Iris</a></i> (2001).
</p><p>The science fiction romance <i><a href="/wiki/Eternal_Sunshine_of_the_Spotless_Mind" title="Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind">Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</a></i> (2004), in which Winslet was cast against <a href="/wiki/Typecasting_(acting)" title="Typecasting (acting)">type</a> in a contemporary setting, proved to be a turning point in her career, and she gained further recognition for her performances in <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Neverland_(film)" title="Finding Neverland (film)">Finding Neverland</a></i> (2004), <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Children_(film)" title="Little Children (film)">Little Children</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Road_(film)" title="Revolutionary Road (film)">Revolutionary Road</a></i> (2008), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Reader_(2008_film)" title="The Reader (2008 film)">The Reader</a></i> (2008). For playing a Nazi camp guard in the last of these, she won the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Leading_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Leading Role">BAFTA Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award</a> for Best Actress. In the 2010s, Winslet played a single mother in 1930s America in the miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Mildred_Pierce_(miniseries)" title="Mildred Pierce (miniseries)">Mildred Pierce</a></i> (2011), joined the <a href="/wiki/The_Divergent_Series" title="The Divergent Series"><i>Divergent</i> film series</a>, and portrayed <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Hoffman" title="Joanna Hoffman">Joanna Hoffman</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs_(film)" title="Steve Jobs (film)">Steve Jobs</a></i> (2015). She won a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Lead_Actress_in_a_Limited_Series_or_Movie" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actress in a Limited Series or Movie">Primetime Emmy Award</a> for the former and a third BAFTA Award for the latter.
</p><p>For her narration of a short story in the audiobook <i>Listen to the Storyteller</i> (1999), Winslet won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Spoken_Word_Album_for_Children" title="Grammy Award for Best Spoken Word Album for Children">Grammy Award</a>. She performed the song "<a href="/wiki/What_If_(Kate_Winslet_song)" title="What If (Kate Winslet song)">What If</a>" for the soundtrack of her film <i><a href="/wiki/Christmas_Carol:_The_Movie" title="Christmas Carol: The Movie">Christmas Carol: The Movie</a></i> (2001). A co-founder of the charity <a href="/wiki/Golden_Hat_Foundation" title="Golden Hat Foundation">Golden Hat Foundation</a>, which aims to create <a href="/wiki/Autism_awareness" class="mw-redirect" title="Autism awareness">autism awareness</a>, she has written a book on the topic, <i>The Golden Hat: Talking Back to Autism</i> (2010). <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine named her one of the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100 most influential people in the world</a> in 2009, and in 2012, she was appointed <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE). Divorced from the film directors <a href="/wiki/Jim_Threapleton" title="Jim Threapleton">Jim Threapleton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Mendes" title="Sam Mendes">Sam Mendes</a>, Winslet has been married to the businessman Ned Rocknroll since 2012. She has a child from each marriage.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_initial_stage_and_television_roles">Early life and initial stage and television roles</span></h2>
<p>Kate Winslet was born on 5 October 1975 in <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading, Berkshire</a>, England, to Sally Anne (<a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9e" class="mw-redirect" title="Née">née</a> Bridges) and Roger John Winslet.<sup id="cite_ref-biography.com_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biography.com-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Her mother worked as a nanny and waitress, and her father, a struggling actor, took labouring jobs to support the family.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-interrupted_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interrupted-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Her maternal grandparents were both actors and ran the Reading Repertory Theatre Company.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Winslet has two sisters, Anna and Beth, both of whom are actresses, and a younger brother, Joss.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The family had limited financial means; they lived on free meal benefits and were supported by a charity named the <a href="/wiki/Actors_Orphanage" title="Actors Orphanage">Actor's Charitable Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> When Winslet was 10, her father severely injured his foot in a boating accident and found it harder to work, leading to more financial hardships for the family.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Winslet has said that her parents always made them feel cared for and that they were a supportive family.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A sign displaying the name of Redroofs Theatre School." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg/220px-Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg/330px-Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg/440px-Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Redroofs_Theatre_School.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Redroofs_Theatre_School" title="Redroofs Theatre School">Redroofs Theatre School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maidenhead" title="Maidenhead">Maidenhead</a>, where Winslet was educated</div></div></div>
<p>Winslet attended St Mary and All Saints' Church of England primary school.<sup id="cite_ref-school_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Living in a family of actors inspired her to pursue acting from a young age.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> She and her sisters participated in amateur stage shows at school and at a local youth theatre, named Foundations.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-interrupted_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interrupted-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> When she was five, Winslet made her first stage appearance as <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Mary</a> in her school's production of the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_of_Jesus" title="Nativity of Jesus">Nativity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-true_love_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-true_love-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> She has described herself as an overweight child; she was nicknamed "blubber" by her schoolmates and was bullied for the way she looked.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> She said that she did not let this defeat her.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> At 11, Winslet was accepted into the <a href="/wiki/Redroofs_Theatre_School" title="Redroofs Theatre School">Redroofs Theatre School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maidenhead" title="Maidenhead">Maidenhead</a>. The school also functioned as an agency and took students to London to audition for acting jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> She appeared in a <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Puffs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar Puffs">Sugar Puffs</a> commercial and dubbed for foreign films.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-premiere_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> At school, she was made <a href="/wiki/Head_girl" class="mw-redirect" title="Head girl">head girl</a> and took part in productions of <i><a href="/wiki/Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland" title="Alice&#39;s Adventures in Wonderland">Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion,_the_Witch_and_the_Wardrobe" title="The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe">The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe</a></i>, and played the lead role of <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Darling" title="Wendy Darling">Wendy Darling</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan_(1954_musical)" title="Peter Pan (1954 musical)">Peter Pan</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> She worked simultaneously with the Starmaker Theatre Company in Reading. She participated in over 20 of their stage productions, but was rarely selected as the lead due to her weight. Nonetheless, she played key roles as Miss Agatha Hannigan in <i><a href="/wiki/Annie_(musical)" title="Annie (musical)">Annie</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Raksha_(The_Jungle_Book)" title="Raksha (The Jungle Book)">Mother Wolf</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jungle_Book" title="The Jungle Book">The Jungle Book</a></i>, and Lena Marelli in <i><a href="/wiki/Bugsy_Malone" title="Bugsy Malone">Bugsy Malone</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991, within two weeks of finishing her <a href="/wiki/GCSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GCSE">GCSE</a> examinations, Winslet made her screen debut as one of the main cast members of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> science fiction television series <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Season" title="Dark Season">Dark Season</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-golden_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcprofile_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcprofile-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Her part was that of Reet, a schoolgirl who helps her classmates fight against a sinister man distributing free computers to her school.<sup id="cite_ref-CornellDay2015_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CornellDay2015-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DochertyMcGown2003_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DochertyMcGown2003-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> She did not earn much from the job, and at 16, a lack of funds forced Winslet to leave Redroofs.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> To support herself, she worked at a delicatessen.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 1992, she had a small part in the television film <i>Anglo-Saxon Attitudes</i>, an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Attitudes" title="Anglo-Saxon Attitudes">Angus Wilson's satirical novel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts2009_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts2009-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Winslet, who weighed 13&#160;stone 3&#160;pounds (84&#160;kg; 185&#160;lb) at the time, played the daughter of an obese woman in it. While filming, an off-hand comment from the director <a href="/wiki/Diarmuid_Lawrence" title="Diarmuid Lawrence">Diarmuid Lawrence</a> about the likeness between her and the actress who played her mother prompted Winslet to lose weight.<sup id="cite_ref-unsinkable_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unsinkable-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> She next took on the role of the young daughter of a bankrupt middle-aged man (played by <a href="/wiki/Ray_Winstone" title="Ray Winstone">Ray Winstone</a>) in the television sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Back_(TV_series)" title="Get Back (TV series)">Get Back</a></i> (1992–93).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> She also had a guest role in a 1993 episode of the medical drama series <i><a href="/wiki/Casualty_(TV_series)" title="Casualty (TV series)">Casualty</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1994.E2.80.931996:_Film_breakthrough"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994–1996:_Film_breakthrough">1994–1996: Film breakthrough</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Jackson01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Peter Jackson looks away from the camera and has a garland over his neck." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Peter_Jackson01.jpg/170px-Peter_Jackson01.jpg" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Peter_Jackson01.jpg/255px-Peter_Jackson01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Peter_Jackson01.jpg/340px-Peter_Jackson01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Jackson01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a> gave Winslet her first film role as a teenage murderess in <i><a href="/wiki/Heavenly_Creatures" title="Heavenly Creatures">Heavenly Creatures</a></i> (1994)</div></div></div>
<p>Winslet was among 175 girls to audition for <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a>'s psychological drama <i><a href="/wiki/Heavenly_Creatures" title="Heavenly Creatures">Heavenly Creatures</a></i> (1994), and was cast after impressing Jackson with the intensity she brought to her part.<sup id="cite_ref-Sibley2006_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sibley2006-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>-based production is based on the <a href="/wiki/Parker%E2%80%93Hulme_murder_case" title="Parker–Hulme murder case">Parker–Hulme murder case</a> of 1954, in which Winslet played <a href="/wiki/Anne_Perry" title="Anne Perry">Juliet Hulme</a>, a teenager who assists her friend, Pauline Parker (played by <a href="/wiki/Melanie_Lynskey" title="Melanie Lynskey">Melanie Lynskey</a>), in the murder of Pauline's mother. She prepared for the part by reading the transcripts of the girls' murder trial, their letters and diaries, and interacted with their acquaintances.<sup id="cite_ref-ways_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ways-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> She has said that she learnt tremendously from the job.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Jackson filmed in the real murder locations, and the experience left Winslet traumatised.<sup id="cite_ref-premiere_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> She found it difficult to detach herself from her character, and said that after returning home, she often cried.<sup id="cite_ref-ways_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ways-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The film was a critical breakthrough for Winslet;<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Desson_Thomson" title="Desson Thomson">Desson Thomson</a> called her "a bright-eyed ball of fire, lighting up every scene she’s in".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Winslet recorded "Juliet's Aria" for the film's soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Also that year, she appeared as Geraldine Barclay, a prospective secretary, in <a href="/wiki/Royal_Exchange,_Manchester" title="Royal Exchange, Manchester">the Royal Exchange Theatre</a> production of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Orton" title="Joe Orton">Joe Orton</a>'s farce <i><a href="/wiki/What_the_Butler_Saw_(play)" title="What the Butler Saw (play)">What the Butler Saw</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While promoting <i>Heavenly Creatures</i> in Los Angeles, Winslet auditioned for the minor part of Lucy Steele for a <a href="/wiki/Sense_and_Sensibility_(film)" title="Sense and Sensibility (film)">1995 film adaptation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen">Jane Austen</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Sense_and_Sensibility" title="Sense and Sensibility">Sense and Sensibility</a></i>, starring and written by <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thompson" title="Emma Thompson">Emma Thompson</a>. Impressed by her reading, Thompson cast her for the much larger part of the recklessly romantic teenager <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Dashwood" title="Marianne Dashwood">Marianne Dashwood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-one_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-one-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The director <a href="/wiki/Ang_Lee" title="Ang Lee">Ang Lee</a> wanted Winslet to play the part with grace and restraint—aspects that he felt were missing from her performance in <i>Heavenly Creatures</i>—and thus asked her to practice <a href="/wiki/Tai_chi" title="Tai chi">tai chi</a>, read <a href="/wiki/Gothic_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic literature">gothic literature</a>, and learn to play the piano.<sup id="cite_ref-one_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-one-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> David Parkinson  of the <i><a href="/wiki/Radio_Times" title="Radio Times">Radio Times</a></i> found Winslet to be a standout among the ensemble cast, and <a href="/wiki/Mick_LaSalle" title="Mick LaSalle">Mick LaSalle</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> took note of how well she had portrayed her character's growth and maturity.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sfgate_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfgate-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The film grossed over US$134 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> She won the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Female_Actor_in_a_Leading_Role" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Leading Role">Screen Actors Guild</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">British Academy Film Award</a> for Best Supporting Actress, and received nominations for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Academy Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Supporting Actress – Motion Picture">Golden Globe Award</a> in the same category.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Also in 1995, Winslet featured in the poorly received <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Disney</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Kid_in_King_Arthur%27s_Court" title="A Kid in King Arthur&#39;s Court">A Kid in King Arthur's Court</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet had roles in two period dramas of 1996—<i><a href="/wiki/Jude_(film)" title="Jude (film)">Jude</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet_(1996_film)" title="Hamlet (1996 film)">Hamlet</a></i>. As with her <i>Heavenly Creatures</i> part, Winslet's roles in these films were those of women with a "mad edge".<sup id="cite_ref-ways_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ways-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Michael_Winterbottom" title="Michael Winterbottom">Michael Winterbottom</a>'s <i>Jude</i>, based on the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Jude_the_Obscure" title="Jude the Obscure">Jude the Obscure</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy" title="Thomas Hardy">Thomas Hardy</a>, she played Sue Bridehead, a young woman with <a href="/wiki/Suffragette" title="Suffragette">suffragette</a> leanings who falls in love with her cousin, Jude (played by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Eccleston" title="Christopher Eccleston">Christopher Eccleston</a>). <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> believed that the part allowed Winslet to display her acting range, and praised her for the defiance she brought to the role.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> After unsuccessfully auditioning for <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Branagh" title="Kenneth Branagh">Kenneth Branagh</a>'s 1994 film <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Shelley%27s_Frankenstein_(film)" title="Mary Shelley&#39;s Frankenstein (film)">Mary Shelley's Frankenstein</a></i>, Winslet was cast for the part of <a href="/wiki/Ophelia_(character)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ophelia (character)">Ophelia</a>, the doomed lover of the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Hamlet" title="Prince Hamlet">title character</a>, in Branagh's adaptation of <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>'s tragedy <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-one_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-one-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Winslet, at 20 years old, was intimidated by the experience of performing Shakespeare with established actors such as Branagh and <a href="/wiki/Julie_Christie" title="Julie Christie">Julie Christie</a>, saying that the job required a level of intellect that she thought she did not possess.<sup id="cite_ref-ways_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ways-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Mike Jeffries of <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> believed that she had played the part "well beyond her years".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Despite the acclaim, <i>Jude</i> and <i>Hamlet</i> earned little at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-box_office_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rt_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rt-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1997.E2.80.932003:_Stardom_with_Titanic_and_small-scale_features"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1997–2003:_Stardom_with_Titanic_and_small-scale_features">1997–2003: Stardom with <i>Titanic</i> and small-scale features</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A picture of Leonardo DiCaprio with his hand raised." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg/170px-Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg" width="170" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg/255px-Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg/340px-Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="749" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_DiCaprio_2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> <i>(pictured)</i> was paired opposite Winslet in <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (1997). A journalist for <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> labelled them "Hollywood’s most iconic screen couple" since <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Bogart" title="Humphrey Bogart">Humphrey Bogart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ingrid_Bergman" title="Ingrid Bergman">Ingrid Bergman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-deneuvely_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deneuvely-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Winslet was keen on playing Rose DeWitt Bukater, a free-spirited socialite aboard the ill-fated <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">RMS <i>Titanic</i></a>, in <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>'s epic romance <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (1997). Cameron was initially reluctant to cast her, preferring the stars <a href="/wiki/Claire_Danes" title="Claire Danes">Claire Danes</a> or <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>, but Winslet pleaded with him, "You don't understand! I am Rose! I don't know why you're even seeing anyone else!"<sup id="cite_ref-www.ew.com_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.ew.com-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Her persistence led Cameron to hire her.<sup id="cite_ref-www.ew.com_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.ew.com-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> featured as her love interest, Jack. <i>Titanic</i> had a production budget of US$200 million, and its arduous principal photography was held at <a href="/wiki/Rosarito_Beach" title="Rosarito Beach">Rosarito Beach</a> where a replica of the ship was created.<sup id="cite_ref-unsinkable_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unsinkable-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Filming proved to be taxing for Winslet. She nearly drowned, caught influenza, suffered from hypothermia on being submerged in freezing water, and had bruises on her arms and knees. The workload allowed her only four hours of sleep per day and she felt drained by the experience.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Ansen" title="David Ansen">David Ansen</a>, writing for <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>, praised Winslet for capturing her character's zeal with delicacy,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and Mike Clark of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> considered her to be the film's prime asset.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Against expectations, <i>Titanic</i> went on to become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">highest-grossing film</a> of all time to that point, earning over US$2 billion in box-office receipts worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-www.ew.com_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.ew.com-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and established Winslet as a global star.<sup id="cite_ref-daft_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daft-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The film won 11 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>—the most for any film—including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> and gained Winslet a <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a> nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet did not view <i>Titanic</i> as a platform for bigger salaries. She eschewed parts in blockbuster films in favour of independent productions that were not widely seen, believing that she "still had a lot to learn" and was unprepared to be a star.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-golden_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-box_office_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> She later said that her decision ensured career longevity.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Hideous_Kinky_(film)" title="Hideous Kinky (film)">Hideous Kinky</a></i>, a low-budget drama shot before the release of <i>Titanic</i>, was Winslet's sole film release of 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-hideous_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hideous-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> She turned down offers to star in <i><a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_in_Love" title="Shakespeare in Love">Shakespeare in Love</a></i> (1998) and <i><a href="/wiki/Anna_and_the_King" title="Anna and the King">Anna and the King</a></i> (1999) to do the film.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Based on the <a href="/wiki/Hideous_Kinky" title="Hideous Kinky">semi-autobiographical novel</a> by <a href="/wiki/Esther_Freud" title="Esther Freud">Esther Freud</a>, <i>Hideous Kinky</i> tells the story of a single British mother yearning for a new life in 1970s Morocco.<sup id="cite_ref-daft_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daft-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hideous_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hideous-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Writing for <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, the critic <a href="/wiki/Janet_Maslin" title="Janet Maslin">Janet Maslin</a> commended Winslet's decision to follow-up <i>Titanic</i> with such an offbeat project, and took note of how well she had captured her character's "obliviousness and optimism".<sup id="cite_ref-hideous_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hideous-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jane_Campion" title="Jane Campion">Jane Campion</a>'s psychological drama <i><a href="/wiki/Holy_Smoke!" title="Holy Smoke!">Holy Smoke!</a></i> (1999) featured Winslet as an Australian woman who joins an Indian religious cult. She found the script brave and was challenged by the idea of portraying an unlikable, manipulative woman.<sup id="cite_ref-daft_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daft-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> She learnt an Australian accent and worked closely with Campion to justify her character's vileness.<sup id="cite_ref-daft_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daft-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The film required her to perform explicit sex scenes with her co-star <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Keitel" title="Harvey Keitel">Harvey Keitel</a>, and featured a scene in which her character appears stark naked and urinates on herself.<sup id="cite_ref-daft_48-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daft-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> David Rooney of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> wrote, "Showing the kind of courage few young thesps would be capable of and an extraordinary range [...] from animal cunning to unhinged desperation, [Winslet] holds nothing back."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> That same year, she voiced a fairy for the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Faeries_(1999_film)" title="Faeries (1999 film)">Faeries</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Spoken_Word_Album_for_Children" title="Grammy Award for Best Spoken Word Album for Children">Grammy Award for Best Spoken Word Album for Children</a> for narrating the short story "The Face in the Lake" for the children's audiobook <i>Listen to the Storyteller</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-grammy_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A head-shot of Judi Dench as she looks directly at the camera." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg/170px-Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg" width="170" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg/255px-Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg/340px-Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="439" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Judi_Dench_at_the_BAFTAs_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Judi_Dench" title="Judi Dench">Judi Dench</a> <i>(pictured)</i> and Winslet played the novelist <a href="/wiki/Iris_Murdoch" title="Iris Murdoch">Iris Murdoch</a> at different ages in <i><a href="/wiki/Iris_(2001_film)" title="Iris (2001 film)">Iris</a></i> (2001).</div></div></div>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Quills" title="Quills">Quills</a></i> (2000), a biopic of the erratic <a href="/wiki/Marquis_de_Sade" title="Marquis de Sade">Marquis de Sade</a>, starring <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Rush" title="Geoffrey Rush">Geoffrey Rush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joaquin_Phoenix" title="Joaquin Phoenix">Joaquin Phoenix</a>, Winslet played the supporting part of a sexually repressed laundress working in a mental asylum.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Hailing her as the "most daring actress working today", James Greenberg of <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_(magazine)" title="Los Angeles (magazine)">Los Angeles</a></i> magazine praised Winslet for "continuing to explore the bounds of sexual liberation".<sup id="cite_ref-Communications2000_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Communications2000-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> She received a SAG Award nomination for Best Supporting Actress.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The following year, she played a fictitious mathematician involved in the cracking of the <a href="/wiki/Enigma_machine" title="Enigma machine">Enigma ciphers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Michael_Apted" title="Michael Apted">Michael Apted</a>'s espionage thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Enigma_(2001_film)" title="Enigma (2001 film)">Enigma</a></i>. Winslet's character was vastly expanded from a subsidiary love-interest in the <a href="/wiki/Enigma_(novel)" title="Enigma (novel)">novel</a> it was based on to a prominent code-breaker in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> She was pregnant while filming, and to prevent this from showing, she wore corsets under her costume.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The biopic <i><a href="/wiki/Iris_(2001_film)" title="Iris (2001 film)">Iris</a></i> (2001) featured Winslet and <a href="/wiki/Judi_Dench" title="Judi Dench">Judi Dench</a> as the novelist <a href="/wiki/Iris_Murdoch" title="Iris Murdoch">Iris Murdoch</a> at different ages. The director <a href="/wiki/Richard_Eyre" title="Richard Eyre">Richard Eyre</a> cast the two actresses after finding a "correspondence of spirit between them".<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Winslet was drawn to the idea of playing an intellectual and zesty female lead, and in research, she read Murdoch's novels, studied <a href="/wiki/John_Bayley_(writer)" title="John Bayley (writer)">her husband</a>'s memoir <i><a href="/wiki/Elegy_for_Iris" title="Elegy for Iris">Elegy for Iris</a></i>, and watched televised interviews of Murdoch.<sup id="cite_ref-iris_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iris-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The project was filmed over four weeks and allowed Winslet to bring her daughter, who was six months old at the time, on set.<sup id="cite_ref-iris_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iris-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Writing for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Amis" title="Martin Amis">Martin Amis</a> commented that "the seriousness and steadiness of [Winslet's] gaze effectively suggest the dawning amplitude of the Murdoch imagination".<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Winslet received her third Oscar nomination for <i>Iris</i>, in addition to BAFTA and Golden Globe nominations for Best Supporting Actress.<sup id="cite_ref-iris_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iris-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet's third film release of 2001 was the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Christmas_Carol:_The_Movie" title="Christmas Carol: The Movie">Christmas Carol: The Movie</a></i>, based on <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a>' <a href="/wiki/A_Christmas_Carol" title="A Christmas Carol">novel</a>. For the film's soundtrack she sang "<a href="/wiki/What_If_(Kate_Winslet_song)" title="What If (Kate Winslet song)">What If</a>", which proved to be a commercial hit; she donated her earnings from it to children's charities.<sup id="cite_ref-singer_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singer-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> After a year-long absence from the screen, Winslet starred as a headstrong journalist interviewing a professor on <a href="/wiki/Death_row" title="Death row">death row</a> in the thriller <i><a href="/wiki/The_Life_of_David_Gale" title="The Life of David Gale">The Life of David Gale</a></i> (2003). She agreed to the project to work with the director <a href="/wiki/Alan_Parker" title="Alan Parker">Alan Parker</a>, whom she admired, and believed that the film raised pertinent questions about capital punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Mick LaSalle thought that the film had muddled the subject and disliked both the film and Winslet's performance.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2004.E2.80.932007:_Romances.2C_comedies.2C_and_Little_Children"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2004–2007:_Romances,_comedies,_and_Little_Children">2004–2007: Romances, comedies, and <i>Little Children</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A casual Kate Winslet looks away from the camera." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg/170px-Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg/255px-Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg/340px-Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="474" data-file-height="715" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_2006_Toronto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet at the <a href="/wiki/2006_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2006 Toronto International Film Festival">2006 Toronto International Film Festival</a></div></div></div>
<p>To avoid typecasting in historical dramas, Winslet sought out films set in contemporary times.<sup id="cite_ref-age_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> She found it in the science fiction romance <i><a href="/wiki/Eternal_Sunshine_of_the_Spotless_Mind" title="Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind">Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</a></i> (2004), in which she played the neurotic and impetuous Clementine, a woman who decides to erase memories of her ex-boyfriend (played by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Carrey" title="Jim Carrey">Jim Carrey</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eternal_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eternal-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Unlike her previous assignments, the role allowed her to display the quirky side to her personality.<sup id="cite_ref-index_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Gondry encouraged Carrey and Winslet to improvise on set, and to keep herself agile she practised kickboxing.<sup id="cite_ref-eternal_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eternal-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> <i>Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</i> proved to be a modest financial success and several critics regarded it as one of the best films of the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> considered it to be a "uniquely funny, unpredictably tender and unapologetically twisted romance" and thought that Winslet was "electrifying and bruisingly vulnerable" in it.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> A journalist for <i><a href="/wiki/Premiere_(magazine)" title="Premiere (magazine)">Premiere</a></i> magazine credited her for abandoning her "corseted English rose persona", and featured it as the 81st greatest film performance of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Winslet considers it to be a favourite among her roles, and she received Best Actress nominations at the Oscar and BAFTA award ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-empire_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empire-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-today_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-today-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> She has said that the film marked a turning point in her career and prompted directors to offer her a wide variety of parts.<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet was paid £6 million to star in her next release of the year, the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Neverland_(film)" title="Finding Neverland (film)">Finding Neverland</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> It is about the relationship between <a href="/wiki/J._M._Barrie" title="J. M. Barrie">J. M. Barrie</a> (played by <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Llewelyn_Davies_boys" title="Llewelyn Davies boys">Llewelyn Davies boys</a>, which inspired Barrie to write <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan" title="Peter Pan">Peter Pan</a>; Winslet played the boys' mother, <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_Llewelyn_Davies" title="Sylvia Llewelyn Davies">Sylvia</a>. Despite her reluctance to star in another period piece, Winslet agreed to the project after empathising with Sylvia's love for her children.<sup id="cite_ref-age_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ella_Taylor" title="Ella Taylor">Ella Taylor</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/LA_Weekly" title="LA Weekly">LA Weekly</a></i> found Winslet to be "radiant and earthy as ever" and <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Paul_Clinton" title="Paul Clinton">Paul Clinton</a> thought that she was "exceptional in a delicate and finely tuned performance".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> She received a second Best Actress nomination at that year's BAFTA Award ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-today_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-today-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> With a box office gross of US$116 million, <i>Finding Neverland</i> became her most widely seen film since <i>Titanic</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-box_office_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, Winslet took on a guest role in an episode of the British comedy sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Extras_(TV_series)" title="Extras (TV series)">Extras</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Merchant" title="Stephen Merchant">Stephen Merchant</a>. She played a satirical version of herself in it—an actress, who in an effort to win an Oscar, takes the role of a nun in a <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a> film.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> She received a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Guest_Actress_in_a_Comedy_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series</a> nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-emmy_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emmy-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Within three months of giving birth to her second child, Winslet returned to work on <i><a href="/wiki/Romance_%26_Cigarettes" title="Romance &amp; Cigarettes">Romance &amp; Cigarettes</a></i>, a musical romantic comedy directed by <a href="/wiki/John_Turturro" title="John Turturro">John Turturro</a>, in which she played Tula, a promiscuous and foulmouthed woman.<sup id="cite_ref-tula_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tula-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The part required her to sing and dance, and it helped her lose weight gained during her pregnancy.<sup id="cite_ref-age_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> She twisted her ankle while filming one of the dance sequences.<sup id="cite_ref-age_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Derek_Elley" title="Derek Elley">Derek Elley</a> of <i>Variety</i> wrote that despite her limited screen time, Winslet had "the showiest role and filthiest one-liners".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Winslet declined an offer from <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a> to star in <i><a href="/wiki/Match_Point" title="Match Point">Match Point</a></i> (2005) to spend more time with her children.<sup id="cite_ref-age_73-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A profile view of Winslet as she speaks into a microphone." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg/170px-Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg/255px-Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg/340px-Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1022" data-file-height="1291" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet at the <a href="/wiki/60th_British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="60th British Academy Film Awards">60th British Academy Film Awards</a>, where she was nominated for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Leading_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Leading Role">Best Actress</a> for her role in <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Children_(film)" title="Little Children (film)">Little Children</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Winslet had four film releases in 2006. She first appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/All_the_King%27s_Men_(2006_film)" title="All the King&#39;s Men (2006 film)">All the King's Men</a></i>, a political thriller set in 1940s <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Sean_Penn" title="Sean Penn">Sean Penn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jude_Law" title="Jude Law">Jude Law</a>. She played the supporting part of the love interest to Law's character.<sup id="cite_ref-empire_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empire-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The film received negative reviews for its lack of political insight and narrative cohesiveness, and failed to recoup its US$55 million investment.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Her next release, the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Children_(film)" title="Little Children (film)">Little Children</a></i>, was better received. Based on <a href="/wiki/Little_Children_(novel)" title="Little Children (novel)">the novel of the same name</a>, the film tells the story of Sarah Pierce, an unhappy housewife who has an affair with a married neighbour (played by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Wilson_(American_actor)" title="Patrick Wilson (American actor)">Patrick Wilson</a>). Winslet was challenged by the role of an uncaring mother, as she did not understand or respect her character's actions.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Scenes requiring her to be hostile towards the child actress playing her daughter proved upsetting for her.<sup id="cite_ref-empire_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empire-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-body_and_soul_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-body_and_soul-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Having given birth to two children, Winslet was anxious about the sex scenes in which she had to be nude; she took on the challenge to present a positive image for women with imperfect bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-body_and_soul_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-body_and_soul-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> wrote that Winslet successfully "registers every flicker of Sarah’s pride, self-doubt and desire, inspiring a mixture of recognition, pity and concern".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> With another Academy Award for Best Actress nomination, Winslet, at 31, became the youngest performer to accrue five Oscar nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After <i>Little Children</i>, Winslet played a part she found more sympathetic in <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Meyers" title="Nancy Meyers">Nancy Meyers</a>' romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Holiday" title="The Holiday">The Holiday</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> She played Iris, a Briton who temporarily <a href="/wiki/Home_exchange" title="Home exchange">exchanges homes</a> with an American (played by <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Diaz" title="Cameron Diaz">Cameron Diaz</a>) during the Christmas holiday season. The film became Winslet's biggest commercial success in nine years, grossing over US$205 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The critic <a href="/wiki/Justin_Chang" title="Justin Chang">Justin Chang</a> thought the film was formulaic yet pleasing, and took note of Winslet's radiance and charm.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In her final release of the year, Winslet voiced Rita, a scavenging sewer rat, in the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Flushed_Away" title="Flushed Away">Flushed Away</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Winslet's sole project of 2007 was as the narrator for the English version of the French children's film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fox_and_the_Child" title="The Fox and the Child">The Fox and the Child</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2008.E2.80.932011:_Awards_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–2011:_Awards_success">2008–2011: Awards success</span></h3>
<p>Winslet had two critically acclaimed roles in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-award09_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award09-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> After reading <a href="/wiki/Justin_Haythe" title="Justin Haythe">Justin Haythe</a>'s screenplay for <i><a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Road_(film)" title="Revolutionary Road (film)">Revolutionary Road</a></i>, an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Yates_(novelist)" title="Richard Yates (novelist)">Richard Yates</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Road" title="Revolutionary Road">debut novel</a>, Winslet recommended the project to her husband at the time, the director <a href="/wiki/Sam_Mendes" title="Sam Mendes">Sam Mendes</a>, and her <i>Titanic</i> co-star Leonardo DiCaprio.<sup id="cite_ref-deneuvely_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deneuvely-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The film traces the tribulations of a young married couple in 1950s suburban America. Winslet was attracted to the idea of playing a woman whose aspirations had not been met,<sup id="cite_ref-guardian08_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian08-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and she read <i><a href="/wiki/The_Feminine_Mystique" title="The Feminine Mystique">The Feminine Mystique</a></i> to understand the psychology of unhappy housewives from the era.<sup id="cite_ref-deneuvely_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deneuvely-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian08_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian08-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Mendes encouraged DiCaprio and Winslet to spend time together, and she believed that the small set they used helped them to develop their character's strained relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-deneuvely_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deneuvely-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Hailing Winslet as "the best English-speaking film actress of her generation", <a href="/wiki/David_Edelstein" title="David Edelstein">David Edelstein</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine wrote that "there isn’t a banal moment in Winslet’s performance—not a gesture, not a word".<sup id="cite_ref-season_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kate Winslet smiles and waves at the camera." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg/170px-KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg" width="170" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg/255px-KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg/340px-KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1087" data-file-height="1903" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KateWinsletAAFeb09.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet at the <a href="/wiki/81st_Academy_Awards" title="81st Academy Awards">81st Academy Awards</a>, where she won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a> award for her performance in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Reader_(2008_film)" title="The Reader (2008 film)">The Reader</a></i> (2008)</div></div></div>
<p>To avoid a scheduling conflict with <i>Revolutionary Road</i>, Winslet turned down an offer to star in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Reader_(2008_film)" title="The Reader (2008 film)">The Reader</a></i>. After her replacement <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman" title="Nicole Kidman">Nicole Kidman</a> left the project due to her pregnancy, Winslet was signed to it.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Directed by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Daldry" title="Stephen Daldry">Stephen Daldry</a>, <i>The Reader</i> is based on <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Schlink" title="Bernhard Schlink">Bernhard Schlink</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Vorleser" class="mw-redirect" title="Der Vorleser">Der Vorleser</a></i> and is about Hanna Schmitz, an illiterate <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camp</a> guard (Winslet), who has an affair with a teenage boy. Winslet researched the Holocaust and the <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> guards. To educate herself on the stigma of illiteracy, she spent time with students at the Literacy Partners, an organisation that teaches adults to read and write.<sup id="cite_ref-huffington_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffington-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Winslet was unable to sympathise with Schmitz and struggled to play the part honestly without humanising her actions.<sup id="cite_ref-award09_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award09-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-huffington_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffington-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, some historians criticised the film for making Schmitz an object of the audience's sympathy and accused the filmmakers of <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_revisionism" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust revisionism">Holocaust revisionism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Todd_McCarthy" title="Todd McCarthy">Todd McCarthy</a> commended her for supplying "a haunting shell to this internally decimated woman", and writing for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>, Sukhdev Sandhu considered her to be "absolutely fearless here, not just in her willingness to expose herself physically, but her refusal to expose her character psychologically".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet received significant awards attention for her performances in <i>Revolutionary Road</i> and <i>The Reader</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> She won a Golden Globe Award for each of these films, and for the latter, she was awarded the Academy Award and <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Leading_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Leading Role">BAFTA Award for Best Actress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-award09_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award09-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> At age 33, she surpassed her own record as the youngest performer to garner six Oscar nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-award09_106-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award09-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> She also became the third actress in history to win two Golden Globe Awards at the same ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Exhausted by the media attention during this period, Winslet took two years off work until she was ready to creatively engage again.<sup id="cite_ref-vogue11_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue11-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet returned to acting with the five-part <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Mildred_Pierce_(miniseries)" title="Mildred Pierce (miniseries)">Mildred Pierce</a></i> (2011), an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Mildred_Pierce" title="Mildred Pierce">James M. Cain's novel</a> from the director <a href="/wiki/Todd_Haynes" title="Todd Haynes">Todd Haynes</a>. It is about the titular heroine (Winslet), a divorcée during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> struggling to establish a restaurant business while yearning for the respect of her narcissistic daughter (played by <a href="/wiki/Evan_Rachel_Wood" title="Evan Rachel Wood">Evan Rachel Wood</a>). Winslet, who had recently divorced Mendes, believed that certain aspects of her character's life mirrored her own.<sup id="cite_ref-vogue11_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue11-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> She was intimidated by the scope of the production, as she featured in every scene of the 280-page script.<sup id="cite_ref-mildred1_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mildred1-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> She was disturbed and upset by the story, and was particularly fascinated by the complex relationship between the mother-daughter pair.<sup id="cite_ref-mildred1_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mildred1-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mildred2_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mildred2-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> She collaborated closely with the production and costume designers, and learnt to bake pies and prepare chickens.<sup id="cite_ref-mildred1_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mildred1-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The broadcast received a limited audience but gained positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Zoller_Seitz" title="Matt Zoller Seitz">Matt Zoller Seitz</a> of <a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon</a> called the series a "quiet, heartbreaking masterpiece" and described Winslet's performance as "terrific—intelligent, focused and seemingly devoid of ego".<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> She received the <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Lead_Actress_in_a_Limited_Series_or_Movie" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actress in a Limited Series or Movie">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actress</a>, in addition to <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Miniseries_or_Television_Film" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Miniseries or Television Film">Golden Globe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award_for_Outstanding_Performance_by_a_Female_Actor_in_a_Miniseries_or_Television_Movie" title="Screen Actors Guild Award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Miniseries or Television Movie">SAG Award</a> wins.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The ensemble thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Contagion_(film)" title="Contagion (film)">Contagion</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Steven_Soderbergh" title="Steven Soderbergh">Steven Soderbergh</a> was Winslet's first film release of 2011. She was cast as a disease detective for the <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">CDC</a>, and she modelled her role on <a href="/wiki/Anne_Schuchat" title="Anne Schuchat">Anne Schuchat</a>, the director of the  <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Immunization_and_Respiratory_Diseases" title="National Center for Immunization and Respiratory Diseases">NCIRD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> <i>Contagion</i> was a commercial success, and <a href="/wiki/David_Denby" title="David Denby">David Denby</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> praised Winslet for capturing the essence of an exasperated woman.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Her next project was the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Polanski" title="Roman Polanski">Roman Polanski</a>-directed <i><a href="/wiki/Carnage_(2011_film)" title="Carnage (2011 film)">Carnage</a></i>, adapted from the play <i><a href="/wiki/God_of_Carnage" title="God of Carnage">God of Carnage</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Yasmina_Reza" title="Yasmina Reza">Yasmina Reza</a>. Set entirely inside an apartment, the <a href="/wiki/Black_comedy" title="Black comedy">black comedy</a> follows two sets of parents feuding over their respective children. <a href="/wiki/Jodie_Foster" title="Jodie Foster">Jodie Foster</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_C._Reilly" title="John C. Reilly">John C. Reilly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Waltz" title="Christoph Waltz">Christoph Waltz</a> co-starred. The cast rehearsed the script like a play for two weeks, and Winslet brought her children with her to Paris for the eight weeks of filming.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Critics found the adaptation to be less compelling than the play, but praised Foster and Winslet's work.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> They both received Golden Globe nominations for it.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.93present:_Critical_disappointments.2C_a_film_series.2C_and_Steve_Jobs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–present:_Critical_disappointments,_a_film_series,_and_Steve_Jobs">2012–present: Critical disappointments, a film series, and <i>Steve Jobs</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Labor_Day_03_(9766118365).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kate Winslet signs autographs." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Labor_Day_03_%289766118365%29.jpg/170px-Labor_Day_03_%289766118365%29.jpg" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Labor_Day_03_%289766118365%29.jpg/255px-Labor_Day_03_%289766118365%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Labor_Day_03_%289766118365%29.jpg/340px-Labor_Day_03_%289766118365%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1927" data-file-height="2705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Labor_Day_03_(9766118365).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet attending the premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Labor_Day_(film)" title="Labor Day (film)">Labor Day</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2013 Toronto International Film Festival">2013 Toronto International Film Festival</a></div></div></div>
<p>Winslet said that her workload of 2011 helped her get over heartbreak from her divorce, and after finishing work on <i>Carnage</i> she took a break from acting to focus on her children.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vogue11_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue11-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> A short part that she had filmed four years earlier for the anthology film <i><a href="/wiki/Movie_43" title="Movie 43">Movie 43</a></i> was her sole screen appearance of 2012, and it received the worst reviews of her career.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Winslet also performed an audiobook recording of <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Zola" title="Émile Zola">Émile Zola</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Raquin" title="Thérèse Raquin">Thérèse Raquin</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> She was reluctant to accept <a href="/wiki/Jason_Reitman" title="Jason Reitman">Jason Reitman</a>'s offer to star in his 2013 <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day_(film)" title="Labor Day (film)">film adaptation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Maynard" title="Joyce Maynard">Joyce Maynard</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Labor_Day_(novel)" title="Labor Day (novel)">Labor Day</a></i>, but agreed after Reitman postponed the production for a year to accommodate Winslet's commitment to her children.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Set over a <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a> weekend, it tells the story of Adele (Winslet), an <a href="/wiki/Agoraphobic" class="mw-redirect" title="Agoraphobic">agoraphobic</a> single mother, who falls in love with an escaped convict. Describing Adele's character as having "more vulnerability than strength", Winslet found her to be a departure from the strong-willed women she typically played.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> A scene in the film required her to make a pie, for which she drew on her baking experience from <i>Mildred Pierce</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Critical reception for the film was negative;<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Chris Nashawaty of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> criticised it as "mawkish and melodramatic" but commended Winslet for adding layers to her passive role.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Winslet earned her tenth Golden Globe nomination for it.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The novelty of playing a villainous part drew Winslet to <a href="/wiki/List_of_The_Divergent_trilogy_characters#Jeanine_Matthews" class="mw-redirect" title="List of The Divergent trilogy characters">Jeanine Matthews</a> in the science fiction film <i><a href="/wiki/Divergent_(film)" title="Divergent (film)">Divergent</a></i> (2014).<sup id="cite_ref-divergent_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divergent-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jeanine_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jeanine-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Set in a dystopian future, the adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Veronica_Roth" title="Veronica Roth">Veronica Roth</a>'s young adult <a href="/wiki/Divergent_(novel)" title="Divergent (novel)">novel</a> stars <a href="/wiki/Shailene_Woodley" title="Shailene Woodley">Shailene Woodley</a> as a heroine fighting an oppressive regime headed by Winslet's character. Winslet was pregnant with her third child while filming, and her tight-fitting costumes had to be altered to accommodate the pregnancy.<sup id="cite_ref-jeanine_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jeanine-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> To maintain her character's intimidating persona, Winslet remained aloof from her co-stars for much of the filming.<sup id="cite_ref-divergent_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divergent-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Richard Lawson of <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> compared the film unfavourably to the <a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_Games_(film_series)" title="The Hunger Games (film series)"><i>Hunger Games</i> film series</a>, and thought that Winslet was underutilised in it.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The film earned US$288 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/A_Little_Chaos" title="A Little Chaos">A Little Chaos</a></i> marked Winslet's return to the period film genre.<sup id="cite_ref-chaos_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chaos-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Directed by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rickman" title="Alan Rickman">Alan Rickman</a>, it is about a rivalry among gardeners commissioned to create a fountain at the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">Palace of Versailles</a>. Winslet's role was that of the fictitious architect Sabine de Barra, someone she believed had overcome extreme grief and hardship like herself.<sup id="cite_ref-chaos_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chaos-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Catherine Shoard of <i>The Guardian</i> took note of the "emotional honesty" Winslet brought to her part, but criticised the implausibility of her role.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Also that year, she read audiobooks of <a href="/wiki/Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl">Roald Dahl</a>'s children's novels <i><a href="/wiki/Matilda_(novel)" title="Matilda (novel)">Matilda</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Finger" title="The Magic Finger">The Magic Finger</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
