</p><p>In 2015, Winslet reprised the role of Jeanine Matthews in the second instalment of the <a href="/wiki/The_Divergent_Series" title="The Divergent Series"><i>Divergent</i> series</a>, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Divergent_Series:_Insurgent" title="The Divergent Series: Insurgent">Insurgent</a></i>, which despite negative reviews earned US$297 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Her next film, an <a href="/wiki/The_Dressmaker_(2015_film)" title="The Dressmaker (2015 film)">adaptation</a> of the Australian gothic novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dressmaker_(Ham_novel)" title="The Dressmaker (Ham novel)">The Dressmaker</a></i>, was described by the director <a href="/wiki/Jocelyn_Moorhouse" title="Jocelyn Moorhouse">Jocelyn Moorhouse</a> as being reminiscent of the western <i><a href="/wiki/Unforgiven" title="Unforgiven">Unforgiven</a></i> (1992).<sup id="cite_ref-dressmaker_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dressmaker-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Winslet starred as the <a href="/wiki/Femme_fatale" title="Femme fatale">femme fatale</a> Tilly Dunnage, a seamstress who returns to her hometown years after she was accused of murder. She learned to sew for the part and designed some of her own costumes.<sup id="cite_ref-dressmaker_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dressmaker-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The production was filmed in the Australian desert and Winslet found it difficult to wear couture dresses in the harsh weather.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Despite disliking the film, Robert Abele of <i>Los Angeles Times</i> commended Winslet for underplaying her over-the-top part.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The film emerged as one of the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Australia#Highest-grossing_Australian_films" title="Cinema of Australia">highest-grossing Australian films</a> of all time, but earned little elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Winslet won an <a href="/wiki/AACTA_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="AACTA Award">AACTA Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/AACTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Leading_Role" title="AACTA Award for Best Actress in a Leading Role">Best Actress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A full side profile of Kate Winslet, as she poses away from the camera." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1642" data-file-height="2782" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_at_2015_TIFF_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2015 Toronto International Film Festival">2015 Toronto International Film Festival</a></div></div></div>
<p>While filming <i>The Dressmaker</i>, Winslet became aware of an upcoming biopic of <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> by <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Sorkin" title="Aaron Sorkin">Aaron Sorkin</a> and directed by <a href="/wiki/Danny_Boyle" title="Danny Boyle">Danny Boyle</a>. Keen to play Jobs' marketing chief and confidant <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Hoffman" title="Joanna Hoffman">Joanna Hoffman</a>, she sent a picture of herself dressed as Hoffman to the film's producer.<sup id="cite_ref-steve_jobs_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steve_jobs-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs_(film)" title="Steve Jobs (film)">Steve Jobs</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Michael_Fassbender" title="Michael Fassbender">Michael Fassbender</a> in the title role, is told in three acts, each depicting a key milestone in Jobs' career. In preparation, Winslet spent time with Hoffman, and worked with a dialect coach to adopt Hoffman's accent, a mixture of Armenian and Polish, which she considered to be the hardest one of her career.<sup id="cite_ref-steve_jobs_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steve_jobs-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The cast rehearsed each act like a play and filmed it in sequence. Winslet collaborated closely with Fassbender, and their off-screen relationship mirrored the collegial dynamic between Jobs and Hoffman.<sup id="cite_ref-steve_jobs_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steve_jobs-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The film received some of the best reviews of Winslet's career but was a box office flop.<sup id="cite_ref-rt_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rt-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Peter Howell of the <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Star" title="Toronto Star">Toronto Star</a></i> commended her for finding "strength and grace" in her part, and Gregory Ellwood of <a href="/wiki/HitFix" title="HitFix">HitFix</a> thought that she had improved on Hoffman's characterisation.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> She won the Golden Globe and BAFTA Awards for Best Supporting Actress, and received her seventh Oscar nomination for it.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Hillcoat" title="John Hillcoat">John Hillcoat</a>'s ensemble crime-thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Triple_9" title="Triple 9">Triple 9</a></i> (2016) featured Winslet as Irina Vlaslov, a ruthless Russian-Israeli gangster.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The critic Ann Hornaday of <i>The Washington Post</i> felt that Winslet had failed to effectively portray her.<sup id="cite_ref-bazaar_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bazaar-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Her next release of the year, <i><a href="/wiki/Collateral_Beauty" title="Collateral Beauty">Collateral Beauty</a></i>, about a man (played by <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a>) struggling with the death of his daughter, was panned by critics.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Writing for <i>New York</i> magazine, Emily Yoshida criticised it as a vacuous remake of <i>A Christmas Carol</i> and wrote that Winslet had "never looked more painted and tired".<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> It was a modest earner at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Winslet agreed to the romantic disaster film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mountain_Between_Us_(film)" title="The Mountain Between Us (film)">The Mountain Between Us</a></i> (2017) to take on the challenge of a role requiring physical exertion.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haunting_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haunting-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> It featured <a href="/wiki/Idris_Elba" title="Idris Elba">Idris Elba</a> and her as two strangers who crash land on an icy, isolated mountain range. They filmed in the mountains of Western Canada at 10,000 feet above sea level where the temperature was well below freezing.<sup id="cite_ref-haunting_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haunting-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Winslet performed her own stunts and described it as the most physically gruelling experience of her career.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Megan Garber praised the chemistry between Elba and Winslet, and Moira Macdonald of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Seattle_Times" title="The Seattle Times">The Seattle Times</a></i> thought that their charisma had enhanced a mediocre picture.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Woody Allen's <i><a href="/wiki/Wonder_Wheel_(film)" title="Wonder Wheel (film)">Wonder Wheel</a></i>, a drama set in 1950s <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island" title="Coney Island">Coney Island</a>, was Winslet's final release of 2017. She played Ginny, a temperamental housewife having an affair with a lifeguard (<a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>). She described Ginny as permanently dissatisfied and uneasy, and playing her proved difficult for Winslet, who suffered from anxiety.<sup id="cite_ref-haunting_167-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haunting-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-variety17_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety17-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manohla_Dargis" title="Manohla Dargis">Manohla Dargis</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> disliked Allen's writing but credited Winslet for filling her "shabby character with feverish life".<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> When asked about her decision to work with Allen despite an allegation of <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen_sexual_assault_allegation" title="Woody Allen sexual assault allegation">child sexual abuse</a> against him, Winslet chose not to comment on Allen's personal life but said that she was pleased with the collaboration.<sup id="cite_ref-haunting_167-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haunting-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Several journalists criticised her decision.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Upcoming_projects">Upcoming projects</span></h4>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_2" title="Avatar 2">Avatar 2</a></i>, a science fiction sequel to James Cameron's <a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">2009 film</a>, which required Winslet to work with <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">motion capture</a> technology, will be released in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-variety17_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety17-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> She learned <a href="/wiki/Freediving" title="Freediving">freediving</a> for her part and was able to hold her breath underwater for seven minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Winslet will next star alongside <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mia_Wasikowska" title="Mia Wasikowska">Mia Wasikowska</a> in <i>Blackbird</i>, a remake of the Danish film <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Heart" title="Silent Heart">Silent Heart</a></i> (2014), directed by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Michell" title="Roger Michell">Roger Michell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> She has also committed to portray the model and photographer <a href="/wiki/Lee_Miller" title="Lee Miller">Lee Miller</a> in an upcoming biopic, and will provide her voice for <i><a href="/wiki/Moominvalley_(TV_series)" title="Moominvalley (TV series)">Moominvalley</a></i>, an animated television series about the <a href="/wiki/Moomins" title="Moomins">Moomins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_work">Humanitarian work</span></h2>
<p>Winslet supports several charities and causes. An orange top she wore in <i>Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</i> was auctioned in 2004 for a fund-raising event at <a href="/wiki/Helen_%26_Douglas_House" title="Helen &amp; Douglas House">Helen &amp; Douglas House</a>, a hospice in Oxford.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, she became a patron of a <a href="/wiki/Gloucester" title="Gloucester">Gloucester</a>-based charity, the Family Haven, which provides counselling services to vulnerable families.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The same year, hand-made envelopes designed by Winslet were auctioned for the "Pushing the Envelope" campaign created by the <a href="/wiki/National_Literacy_Trust" title="National Literacy Trust">National Literacy Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Winslet was one of the celebrities to participate in a 2007 auction to raise funds for the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_Relief_Organization" title="Afghanistan Relief Organization">Afghanistan Relief Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, she contributed to the Butterfly Book, a compilation of doodles made by several celebrities, to raise money for leukaemia research.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kate Winslet speaks into a microphone." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg/220px-Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg/330px-Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg/440px-Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2431" data-file-height="2626" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kate_Winslet_Palm_Film_Festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Palm_Springs_International_Film_Festival" title="Palm Springs International Film Festival">Palm Springs International Film Festival</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 2009, Winslet narrated the English version of an Icelandic documentary named <i>A Mother's Courage: Talking Back to Autism</i>, about Margret Ericsdottir, whose child Keli Thorsteinsson has non-verbal <a href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autism</a>. Inspired by the story, she teamed with Ericsdottir in 2010 to form an NGO named the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Hat_Foundation" title="Golden Hat Foundation">Golden Hat Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-confident_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-confident-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The organisation aims to create <a href="/wiki/Autism_awareness" class="mw-redirect" title="Autism awareness">autism awareness</a> and was named after a poem written by Thorsteinsson.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> As the brand ambassador of the luxury brands <a href="/wiki/Lanc%C3%B4me" title="Lancôme">Lancôme</a> and <a href="/wiki/Longines" title="Longines">Longines</a>, Winslet partnered with these companies to raise awareness and funds for the foundation. She created a make-up collection for Lancôme in 2011 and, in 2017, she designed a new watch for Longines.<sup id="cite_ref-confident_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-confident-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Winslet wrote a book about autism, entitled <i>The Golden Hat: Talking Back to Autism</i>, which was published by <a href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Schuster" title="Simon &amp; Schuster">Simon &amp; Schuster</a>. It contains correspondence between Winslet and Ericsdottir, personal statements from various celebrities, and contributions from Thorsteinsson.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> A reviewer for <i><a href="/wiki/Publishers_Weekly" title="Publishers Weekly">Publishers Weekly</a></i> praised the book for its "warmth and sincerity".<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> featured the book during a ceremony on the <a href="/wiki/World_Autism_Awareness_Day" title="World Autism Awareness Day">World Autism Awareness Day</a> of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> For her work with the Golden Hat Foundation, Winslet received Spain's Yo Dona award for Best Humanitarian Work.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet narrated a video for <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a> in 2010 that showed animal cruelty in the production of <a href="/wiki/Foie_gras" title="Foie gras">foie gras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> She encouraged chefs to remove the item from their menu and urged consumers to boycott it.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Winslet lent her support to the <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> campaign World’s Largest Lesson, which creates awareness among children about <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Global_citizenship" title="Global citizenship">global citizenship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Teased as a child for her weight, Winslet takes a stand against body-shaming and bullying.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> She narrated an Australian animated short film named <i>Daisy Chain</i> (2015), about a victim of cyber-bullying.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Winslet teamed with Leonardo DiCaprio's environmental foundation for a fundraiser on global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Also that year, DiCaprio and Winslet auctioned off a private dinner with themselves to raise money for a British woman's cancer treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Winslet teamed with Lancôme and the National Literacy Trust in 2018 to launch a programme that aims to educate underprivileged women in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>While filming <i>Dark Season</i>, Winslet, aged 15, began a romantic relationship with the actor-writer <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Tredre" title="Stephen Tredre">Stephen Tredre</a>, who was 12 years her senior.<sup id="cite_ref-premiere_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-waving_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waving-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> She considered him to be a major influence in her life and cohabited with him in London.<sup id="cite_ref-interrupted_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interrupted-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unsinkable_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unsinkable-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The couple separated in 1995, but they remained close until he died of <a href="/wiki/Bone_cancer" class="mw-redirect" title="Bone cancer">bone cancer</a> two years later.<sup id="cite_ref-premiere_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Winslet missed the premiere of <i>Titanic</i> to attend his funeral.<sup id="cite_ref-queen_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-queen-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> In a 2008 interview, she said that she had never gotten over his death.<sup id="cite_ref-interrupted_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interrupted-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Labor_Day_06_(9766132966)_(cropped_2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A pregnant Kate Winslet poses for the camera." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Labor_Day_06_%289766132966%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/170px-Labor_Day_06_%289766132966%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Labor_Day_06_%289766132966%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/255px-Labor_Day_06_%289766132966%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Labor_Day_06_%289766132966%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/340px-Labor_Day_06_%289766132966%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1391" data-file-height="2028" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Labor_Day_06_(9766132966)_(cropped_2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet, pregnant with her third child, in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>A year after Tredre's death, Winslet met <a href="/wiki/Jim_Threapleton" title="Jim Threapleton">Jim Threapleton</a> on the set of <i>Hideous Kinky</i>, in which he was an assistant director.<sup id="cite_ref-waving_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waving-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-queen_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-queen-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> They married in November 1998 at her primary school in Reading, and she gave birth to their daughter, Mia, in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-school_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-premiere_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Describing her marriage to Threapleton as a "mess", she later said that she had lost control of her instincts during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-index_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> They divorced in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-divorce_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divorce-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-glamour_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glamour-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Soon after separating from Threapleton, Winslet met the director <a href="/wiki/Sam_Mendes" title="Sam Mendes">Sam Mendes</a> when he offered her a part in a play. She refused the offer but began dating him.<sup id="cite_ref-golden_couple_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden_couple-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Disillusioned by the way the British tabloids portrayed her personal life, Winslet moved to New York.<sup id="cite_ref-index_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> She wed Mendes in May 2003 on the island of <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-interrupted_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interrupted-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mendes_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mendes-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Their son, Joe, was born later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-mendes_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mendes-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The family divided their time in New York with frequent visits to their estate in the <a href="/wiki/Cotswolds" title="Cotswolds">Cotswolds</a> in England.<sup id="cite_ref-golden_couple_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden_couple-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Amid intense media speculation of an affair between Mendes and the actress <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Hall" title="Rebecca Hall">Rebecca Hall</a>, the couple announced their separation in 2010 and were divorced a year later.<sup id="cite_ref-vogue11_116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue11-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Winslet admitted to being heartbroken by the split, but affirmed her determination to look after her children in spite of her marital breakups.<sup id="cite_ref-bazaar11_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bazaar11-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While holidaying at <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>'s estate on <a href="/wiki/Necker_Island_(British_Virgin_Islands)" title="Necker Island (British Virgin Islands)">Necker Island</a> in 2011, Winslet met her third husband, Ned Rocknroll (born Edward Abel Smith; he is the nephew of Branson and works for <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Galactic" title="Virgin Galactic">Virgin Galactic</a>), during a house fire.<sup id="cite_ref-steve_jobs_154-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steve_jobs-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The couple married in New York in December 2012, and their son, Bear, was born the next year.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> After moving back to England, Winslet purchased a property worth £3.25 million by the sea in <a href="/wiki/West_Wittering" title="West Wittering">West Wittering</a>, Sussex, where (as of 2015) she lives with Rocknroll and her children.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> In a 2015 interview, she described how much she enjoyed living in the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-bazaar_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bazaar-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet has said that despite her three marriages and a family structure that might be perceived as "unconventional" by some, she does not consider it to be any "less of a family".<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> She refuses jobs that take her away from her children for long, and likes to schedule her film commitments to coincide with their school holidays.<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Discussing her parenting style, Winslet remarked that she enjoys packing lunches and doing the school run.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<p>Several journalists consider Winslet to be among the best actresses of her generation.<sup id="cite_ref-deneuvely_42-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deneuvely-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-award09_106-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award09-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-actors_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actors-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Despite achieving stardom early in her career with the top-grossing <i>Titanic</i>, Winslet has rarely acted in commerce-driven pictures.<sup id="cite_ref-steve_jobs_154-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steve_jobs-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-njcom_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-njcom-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> A journalist for <i>Elle</i> believes that her choices reflect the "soul and attitude of a jobbing actress, trapped in the body of a movie star".<sup id="cite_ref-elle04_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elle04-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Perrotta" title="Tom Perrotta">Tom Perrotta</a>, the author of <i>Little Children</i>, has said that Winslet "gravitates toward troubling roles in smaller films", typically those of "thorny, potentially unsympathetic" women.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> The journalist <a href="/wiki/Mark_Harris_(journalist)" title="Mark Harris (journalist)">Mark Harris</a> writes that she specialises in "unsentimentalized, restless, troubled, discontented, disconcerted, difficult women" and John Hiscock of <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> has identified a theme of characters who are free-spirited with a sexual edge to them.<sup id="cite_ref-true_love_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-true_love-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-award09_106-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award09-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Stephen Whitty of <a href="/wiki/NJ.com" title="NJ.com">NJ.com</a> associates Winslet with "serious, almost despairing material", although he finds it hard to pigeonhole her as an actress.<sup id="cite_ref-njcom_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-njcom-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:20%;&#32;; background-color: #E0E6F8;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"I can't just learn my lines and do [my job], but perhaps that's because I don't want to act, I want to be. And I do think there's a difference."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">&#160;– Winslet on acting<sup id="cite_ref-njcom_219-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-njcom-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Leonardo DiCaprio, who starred with Winslet in <i>Titanic</i> and <i>Revolutionary Road</i>, considers her to be "the most prepared and well-researched actor on set", and Jude Law, her co-star in <i>The Holiday</i>, believes that despite her seriousness she remains "very calm and good-natured".<sup id="cite_ref-vogue11_116-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue11-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vogue07_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue07-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Her <i>Steve Jobs</i> director Danny Boyle has identified a willingness in Winslet to avoid typecasting and has said that she takes an effort "to reposition directors’ and producers’ perspective on her" to allow herself to be challenged as an artist.<sup id="cite_ref-steve_jobs_154-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steve_jobs-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet has said that she is interested in parts of "angst-ridden women" with strong dispositions masking flaws and insecurities.<sup id="cite_ref-award09_106-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-award09-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haunting_167-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haunting-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> She connects with "women who are either finding their way out of a situation, looking for love, having some struggle within love, or questioning the big things in life".<sup id="cite_ref-bedtime_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedtime-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Drawn to parts that are in tandem with her personal struggles at certain points in her life,<sup id="cite_ref-hrinterview_5-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrinterview-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> she finds it difficult to detach herself from her roles, saying that "you have to confront your true feelings every single day. And that’s pretty exhausting. Then you have to go home and make dinner".<sup id="cite_ref-njcom_219-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-njcom-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vogue07_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue07-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Even so, she finds it therapeutic to perform.<sup id="cite_ref-vogue11_116-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue11-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Winslet is known for her willingness to perform nude scenes, having done so in 12 of her films, although she considers its contribution to the narrative before agreeing to it.<sup id="cite_ref-steve_jobs_154-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steve_jobs-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> She believes that these scenes promote a positive body image among women.<sup id="cite_ref-vogue12_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue12-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span></h2>
<p>In a 2015 article for <i><a href="/wiki/Elle_(magazine)" title="Elle (magazine)">Elle</a></i>, Sally Holmes described Winslet's ability to establish rapport with her manner.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Jo Ellison of <i>Vogue</i> writes that she has an "authoritative, almost ambassadorial aura", and <a href="/wiki/Kira_Cochrane" title="Kira Cochrane">Kira Cochrane</a> of <i>The Guardian</i> considers her to be "articulate, sophisticated, [with] a definite hint of grandeur".<sup id="cite_ref-guardian08_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian08-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vogue11_116-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue11-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Describing Winslet as plain-spoken, Krista Smith of <i>Vanity Fair</i> believes that despite her stardom she is unpretentious.<sup id="cite_ref-deneuvely_42-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deneuvely-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A bust shot of Kate Winslet." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg/170px-KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg/255px-KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg/340px-KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1327" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KateWinsletByAndreaRaffin2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winslet at the <a href="/wiki/68th_Venice_International_Film_Festival" title="68th Venice International Film Festival">2011 Venice International Film Festival</a></div></div></div>
<p>Winslet's weight fluctuations over the years have been well documented by the media.<sup id="cite_ref-waving_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waving-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pomerance2011_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pomerance2011-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> She has been outspoken about her refusal to allow Hollywood to dictate her weight.<sup id="cite_ref-golden_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deneuvely_42-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deneuvely-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, the British edition of <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> magazine published photographs of Winslet that had been digitally altered to make her look taller and thinner.<sup id="cite_ref-GilmanGilman2008_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GilmanGilman2008-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Winslet stated that the alterations were made without her consent.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> <i>GQ</i> subsequently issued an apology.<sup id="cite_ref-golden_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, she won a defamation case against <i><a href="/wiki/Grazia" title="Grazia">Grazia</a></i> magazine after it claimed that she had visited a dietitian.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> She claimed £10,000 in damages, and donated the amount to an eating disorder charity.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> She won another case in 2009 against the British tabloid <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> after it claimed she had lied about her exercise regimen.<sup id="cite_ref-libel_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libel-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> She received an apology and a payout of £25,000.<sup id="cite_ref-libel_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libel-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet was named one of the most beautiful people in the world by <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> magazine in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Her beauty and sex appeal have been picked up by several other publications, including <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Bazaar" title="Harper&#39;s Bazaar">Harper's Bazaar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Who_(magazine)" title="Who (magazine)">Who</a></i>, and <i>Empire</i> magazines.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> She has said that she does not subscribe to the beauty ideal of Hollywood, and uses her celebrity to empower women to accept their appearance with pride.<sup id="cite_ref-vogue12_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogue12-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> She has spoken against <a href="/wiki/Botox" class="mw-redirect" title="Botox">Botox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plastic_surgery" title="Plastic surgery">plastic surgery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> In an effort to encourage natural ageing, she formed the British Anti-Cosmetic Surgery League, alongside the actresses Emma Thompson and <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Weisz" title="Rachel Weisz">Rachel Weisz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> She instructs magazines and brands not to digitally smooth her wrinkles in photographs.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Winslet is reluctant to discuss the <a href="/wiki/Gender_pay_gap" title="Gender pay gap">gender pay gap</a> in Hollywood as she dislikes talking about her salary in public.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes (magazine)">Forbes</a></i> reported her annual salary to be US$2 million, a majority of that stemming from her endorsement deals.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Also that year, the <a href="/wiki/UK_Film_Council" title="UK Film Council">UK Film Council</a> calculated that she had earned £20 million from her acting roles since 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine named Winslet one of the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100 most influential people in the world</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Time100_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time100-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> in London unveiled a wax statue of Winslet in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> The following year, she received an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_C%C3%A9sar" title="Honorary César">Honorary César</a> award, and in 2014, she received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Winslet was appointed <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Birthday_Honours" title="2012 Birthday Honours">2012 Birthday Honours</a> for her services to drama.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_credits_and_awards">Acting credits and awards</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Kate_Winslet_performances" title="List of Kate Winslet performances">List of Kate Winslet performances</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Kate_Winslet" title="List of awards and nominations received by Kate Winslet">awards and nominations</a></div>
<p>Prolific in film since 1994, Winslet's most acclaimed and highest-grossing films, according to the online portal <a href="/wiki/Box_Office_Mojo" title="Box Office Mojo">Box Office Mojo</a> and the review aggregate site <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, include <i><a href="/wiki/Heavenly_Creatures" title="Heavenly Creatures">Heavenly Creatures</a></i> (1994), <i><a href="/wiki/Sense_and_Sensibility_(film)" title="Sense and Sensibility (film)">Sense and Sensibility</a></i> (1995), <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet_(1996_film)" title="Hamlet (1996 film)">Hamlet</a></i> (1996), <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (1997), <i><a href="/wiki/Eternal_Sunshine_of_the_Spotless_Mind" title="Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind">Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</a></i> (2004), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Holiday" title="The Holiday">The Holiday</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Divergent_(film)" title="Divergent (film)">Divergent</a></i> (2014), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Divergent_Series:_Insurgent" title="The Divergent Series: Insurgent">Insurgent</a></i> (2015), and <i><a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs_(film)" title="Steve Jobs (film)">Steve Jobs</a></i> (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-box_office_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rt_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rt-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Her television projects include the miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Mildred_Pierce_(miniseries)" title="Mildred Pierce (miniseries)">Mildred Pierce</a></i> (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-mildred1_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mildred1-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Winslet has been recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Motion_Picture_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences">Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences</a> for the following performances:<sup id="cite_ref-awards_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awards-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/68th_Academy_Awards" title="68th Academy Awards">68th Academy Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Best Supporting Actress</a>, nomination, for <i>Sense and Sensibility</i> (1995)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/70th_Academy_Awards" title="70th Academy Awards">70th Academy Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a>, nomination, for <i>Titanic</i> (1997)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/74th_Academy_Awards" title="74th Academy Awards">74th Academy Awards</a>: Best Supporting Actress, nomination, for <i><a href="/wiki/Iris_(2001_film)" title="Iris (2001 film)">Iris</a></i> (2001)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/77th_Academy_Awards" title="77th Academy Awards">77th Academy Awards</a>: Best Actress, nomination, for <i>Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</i> (2004)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/79th_Academy_Awards" title="79th Academy Awards">79th Academy Awards</a>: Best Actress, nomination, for <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Children_(film)" title="Little Children (film)">Little Children</a></i> (2006)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/81st_Academy_Awards" title="81st Academy Awards">81st Academy Awards</a>: Best Actress, win, for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Reader_(2008_film)" title="The Reader (2008 film)">The Reader</a></i> (2008)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards" title="88th Academy Awards">88th Academy Awards</a>: Best Supporting Actress, nomination, for <i>Steve Jobs</i> (2015)</li></ul>
<p>Winslet has won three <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">BAFTA Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Leading_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Leading Role">Best Actress</a> for <i>The Reader</i> (2008); and <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">Best Supporting Actress</a> for <i>Sense and Sensibility</i> (1995) and <i>Steve Jobs</i> (2016).<sup id="cite_ref-awards_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awards-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> She has also won the <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Lead_Actress_in_a_Limited_Series_or_Movie" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actress in a Limited Series or Movie">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actress in a Miniseries</a> for <i>Mildred Pierce</i> (2011), and the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Spoken_Word_Album_for_Children" title="Grammy Award for Best Spoken Word Album for Children">Grammy Award for Best Spoken Word Album for Children</a> for narrating the children's audiobook <i>Listen to the Storyteller</i> (1999).<sup id="cite_ref-grammy_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-emmy_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emmy-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> She is among the few actresses to win three of the four major American entertainment awards (<a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_won_Academy,_Emmy,_Grammy,_and_Tony_Awards" title="List of people who have won Academy, Emmy, Grammy, and Tony Awards">EGOT</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
